14/20/2000
SECRET
Echward C. Tichboro
Mr.
Dear Mr.
Tichboro
Reference is made to your current contract with the United States
Governament, as represented by the Contracting Officer.
Arrangements have been recently completed allowing certain
independent contractors of this organisation to obtain social accuritv
credits by covering such individuals under the social security tax
provisions applicable to employees. These arrangements also include
a provision for retroactive applicability to the beginning of the
1965 tax year. This can be done only for reasons of security since
the procedure results in reducing the social security tax from the
self-employed rate to the employee rate. For example, in January
of 1965 the tax rates were 5.4% and 3-5/8% respectively.
As a consequence thereof, said contract is amended by deloting
all reference to social security and by adding the following paragraph:
"Effertive 1 December 1964, social security taxes will be covertly
deducted by this-organisation from your compensation in the same
manner and to the same extent as would be done if you were a Govern-
ment employee. Security reasons make this procedure necessary. Its
implementation does not imply in any manner the actual creation of an
employee-employer relationship. Your legal status under this agree-
ment continues to be that of an independent contractor.
If you receive or expect to receive full or partial social security
credits from overt sources you will so notify this organization and an
adjustment will be made or covert deductiono discontinued, depending
upon the circumstances Further, if you should subsequently receive
overt social socurity credits, evidence thereof will be submitted to this
organisation. In such event your covert credits will be erased and your
covert deductions returned.
All other terms and conditions of sal contract remain in full force
and effect.
UNITED STATES GOVERNMENT
SIGNED
BY
Contracting Cificor

SUBJECT
SUBJECT
Overdue 1964 Covert Income Tax Returns
ACTION REQUIRED. REFERENCE
Action Required: Priority
The following -agents in Mexico City are delinquent in
the filing of their 1964 Covert Income Tax returns. You
are requested to obtain these outstanding returns as soon
as possible since delinquent tax returns are subject to 6%
statutory interest on the unpaid tax due from 15 April to
the date of payment, and in addition are also subject to a
penalty of 5% per month, not to exceed 25% of the tax liability.
Jormy K. BENADUM

10 June 1965
MEMORANDUM FOR: CI/QA
ATTENITICE
:
Mr. Lally
SUBJECT
:
Edvard G. TICBORN (201-253203)
REFERENCES
:
CI/QA Memorandum of 33 June 1964
CI/QA Memorandum of 3 June 1961
1. All of the information requested on Subject has now
been submitted to your office. Project LICOLIC, which provides
support for TICBORN, describes Subject's duties as follows:
a. Subject moves in Mexican leftist and Marxist
intellectual circles with a good range of associations in this
million; in this context, he has successfully developed and now
publishes an intellectual magazine under Station direction.
b. Re is available to the WH Division for travel to
other Latin American countries for political assessments or
for ad hoc assignments involving contact with local political
figures of interest.
c. He is used to handle dissident or disaffected
Communists or far leftists where contacts are required by
other Stations and where CA objectives are involved.
2. It is requested that a new QA on Subject be expedited.
W. J. Kaufmann
Chief, WH/1

ACTION REQUIRED - RESENCIES
REFERENCE: 1815-3432, 22 April 1964
1. The delay in answering reference should not be construed no leck
of desire or intent, on the part of TICERION or the Chief of Station,
that the case be surlditted to the Cardi of Review for Sertames and Losses
for consideration, but rather as an administrative delay of getting the facts,
people, papers, etc., together and in the place for submission.
2. Attached is a statement prepared by TICEROU regarding the loss
of funds and containing the pertinent circumstances of the case. The
sub-arrarship numberings are in accordance with, and relating to, the
requirements of paragraph 3, a of R1 34-250. The information requested
in sub-arrarships numbered 8 through 12 43 as expressed jointly by Stewart
R. PARKET and Jeremy J. TALISIS who were assirated to investigate the matter
by the Board of Directors.
3. PATATER and MALSIS talked with TICEROU; at different times,
regarding the shortage of funds and the inferences as related to them
were substantially the same as outlined in TICEROUN's statement. Since
there is no other way to verify the facts and TICEROU can be proven herself
to be truthful and forthright in his dealings with the Station his
statement regarding the loss of fuxis is accepted as fact.
4. Since TICEROUN in authorized travel exercise "on actinil,
reasonable, and necessary expense basis" it does not seem sensible for
his to have reported the loss of funds in other than the key he says
actually happened.

INCORPERS
SUBJECT
Contract Amendment Edward G. TICHBORN
ACTION REQUIRIO REJECTORS
Reference: DIB 67851
Action Required: FYI
1. Forwarded berewith is the referenced amendment
Edward G. TICHBORN's contract which provides for a one year
extension effective 19 November 1964 and a compensation
increase from $9,000 to $12,000.
2. During Subject's recent TDY in Washington it was
made clear to him that this substantial pay raise and extension
of his contract was on the basis that TICHBORN continue to
devote 85 to 90% of his time to KUBARK activity. In view of
the fact that Subject is currently handling only one intellectual
property. The proposed agreement was to be made to the extent
that his work load reverts to the 50 to 65% level, he cannot
expect to continue to receive the present amount of compensation.
During Subject's talks at Hoadquarters, it appeared that
the 100% of the 100% of the 100% of the 100% of the 100% of
he is reaffidered on the basis of services rendered, In return
for this arrangement, the government makes no claim on income
he might receive from his private business activities. Obviously
it is our hope that coupled with the occasional full-time
assignments in other WH countries levied on TICHBORN, that the
Station will be able to continue to utilize Subject's services
at the high level of activity which will justify his current
compensation.
MICROFILMCS
MAR 24 1955
Chester D. DAINOLD
Doc. MICRO. BEA.

Amendment; h.w.

ACCOPIUM
SHORT
General - Administrative
Specific - Cover Income Tax Return to Edward G. TICBOARD
ACTION HOUND: DEFERENCE
REFERENCE: BDS-3952, dated 15 January 1965
1. Refranced dispatch has caused TICHBORN and the Station to become aware
of some own problems with the Maxican banking system. As Headquarters may
not be aware, TICBORN has a dollar account with a Mexico City bank for his
personal affairs. Insurance, insurance, insurance, insurance, insurance, insurance
depository, and insurance insurance. TICHBORN requested his bank to
depository, but only provide atatemente. TICHBORN requested his bank to
provide him with his cancelled check (on a loan basis) so that copies could
be made of it. It developed over a process of several weeks that the bank
could be made of it. It would not had it been run through TICHBORN's account,
Sliace ample time had expired. The bank is held in June 1964), the bank checked
all accounts of persons with TICHBORN's account name on the theory that it
might have been run through cosmome else's account (not an unusual occurrence
here). If had not that the bank could discogred.
2. As a result, TICHBORN is stopping payment on the check with the bank,
writing the office with which he filed his overt income tax, advising that
office of the circumstances, and requesting some word back whether or not,
the check was made to the bank and the check. If the check was
received, TICHBORN will provide the State of the City and the City's
stating and remove the "stop payment" order on the check. If the check was
not received (mail is another problem), then TICHBORN will send another check
and a copy of the interchange of correspondence on the matter with the bank
and the Income tax authorities will be provided Headquarters. It is hoped
this will be satisfactory.
3. The only reason the Station is providing all the grouscoma details on the
foregoing to so that Headquarters will have some understanding of the Mexican
banking problems should questions of this nature arise again.
for
Willard c. CURTIS

Dear F..Thomee:
Due to increased demands unon my time from other clients,
I find it necessary to relinquish my duties as legal counsel
for the IILR here in Mexico, and I do so with great reluctance.
One of my heretofore-leaser clients has recently expended his
activities in certain resl estte developments in Gundalajara
and Puerto Vallarta, thereby necessitating 4 frequent absence
from Mexico City. Then, too, I had underestimated the amount
of tine and effort required to satisfactorily attend the verious
legal and administrative matters confronting CEDS. Should you
so desire, I could recommend other legal counsel; but I am
inclined to feel that the Centro's principal problems would be
of an administrative nature rather then a legal one.
As for my legal fees to date, I am submitting a bill for
$650.00 U.S. C.7. This represents a total of 65 hours at the
rate of $10.00 per hour. By regular fees count to $20.00 per
hour, but, in keeping with my own political affinity for labor
courses, I have reduced them to the lesser figure.
My I thank you again for your confidence and good will in
having chosen me as legal counsel for your org-nization's activities
in Mexico. I shall be happy to give you a personal report of my
observations on my next trip to New York.
Sincerely yours,
Henry P. Lopez

3. Taking all the foregoing into consideration and to avoid complications with
his present projects up TICIBORN, the Station asked him what understanding he
had so the proportion of his time to be devoted to KUBARK activities, lie said
that his present contract was predicated on approximately 60 to 66-2/3% of
his time being utilized by KUBARK. His present estimate is that he is devoting
85 to 90% of his time to KUBARK activities; and, if he is to do the kind of job
that is desired on the two intellectual projects recently acquired, he will
be the same as the KUBARK. Of course, he continues to be available for appropriate
election of political assets (such as FUSPEN) in other countries from time
to time; but, it has to be recorded and that when he is absent from basic,
this represents 100% of his time.
4. The Station agrees with his analysis on current commitments against his
timn on behalf of KUBARK. Therefore, it was indicated to TICIBORN that he
should be prepared to take up this matter with Headquarters at the time he
makes his late October trip to PERRINE in connection with the new intellectual
magazine (see reference) and that the Station would request Headquarters to be
prepared to dedicuss the state of the State of Virginia. Section's understanding
of the State's contract extension expires 19 November 1986.
5. The Station would like to emphasize that this matter was brought up at its
initiative in order to try (n) to assure that demands being placed on TICIBORN
recently could be reasonably expected to be fulfilled and (b) to get a complete
understanding on all aspects of TICIBORN's contractual status fritten and
unwritten) so that neither the Station nor TICIBORN get committed to these
continuing activities and suddenly find themselves in contention about the
time/salary-involed it. should also be emphasized that TICIBORN has not
complained about recent requirements but has devoted whatever time required
to handle them and do the job expected.

SECRET.
13 June 1963
MEMORANDUM FOR: Chief, Contract Personal Division
SUBJECT:
Edward G. TICHBORN (p), Amendment
of Contract
1. It is requested that the contract, as amended for
Edward G. TICHBORN; Contract Agent, be further amended effec-
tive 1 June 1963 as follows:
a. Increase basic compensation from '80,000
to $9,000 per annum.
b. Provide additional compensation for quar-
ters procurement at the rate of $3,000 per annum
for self and dependents.
Extend the period of the contract for an
additional year.
d. All other provisions of the contract remain
in effect.
2. The increase in compensation as recommended by the
Vexico City Station is based on the manner of TICHBORN's par-
formance and the increased amount of time which the d'avotes
to Agency requirements.
3. The WH Division concurs with the Station recommenda-
tion. TICHBORN has becona an increasingly valuable and pro-
ductive covert asset.
W. E. BROOKS
Chief, WH-Support

CONTINUATION OF
DISPATCH
S F. C R E T R I D A T
16.
H. Haedquarters suggests that than TICHERCH'S contrast is renoved
as of 19 May 1963 for two years, it be amended to increase his salary by
$1,000 par year, and that additional compensation of $3,500 per year be
included for housing. The whole amount would be taxable. A clause on
also be added to the contract authorising TINBROEN to apply for the special
life and hospitalisation insurance given Contract Agents.
5. Please discuss the proposal in paragraph 4 and/or any Station
ideas with TICHERCH, but avoid making any commitments. Since the present
contract carries on 19 May, it is requested that the Station able ite views
on TICHERCH's future use and proper pay.

PAPU
Chief of Station, Caracas
FROM
Chief of Station, Mexico City
SUBJECT
Tichborn Report on Caracas Travel
ACTION REPORTS
Reference: IDWV-11415, 22 March 1963 5:13
1. Station Review regrets that, to date, it has been unable
to obtain the Reference Report from Tichborn. As headquarters is aware,
Tichborn, while brilliant and articulate, is not always dependable,
especially when it comes to routine tasks. It is true, however, that
Tichborn has been extremely busy traveling for KUBARK, and is at the moment
on another of his frequent trips.
2. In any event, Tichborn has promised to provide the report as
soon as he returns from his present trip. It will be forwarded when received
from him.
RECLASSIFIED.

20 March 1963
REIDOTANDUN POR: Chior, Contract Personal Division
SUBJECT:
Edward 0. TICHBORN (p), Contract Amendment
1. It is requested that the contract for Edward 0. TICHBORN,
Contract Agent, be amended to delete the current paragraph 2.
Travel and Operational Expenses and insert:
"2. Travel and Operational Expenses. You will be
advanced or reimbursed funds on an actual, reasonable
and necessary expense has been made to incurred
for the purpose of being through travel or may be directed
or authorised by the Government and while on temerory
duty away from your permanent post of assignment. in
addition, you will be advanced or reimbursed funds for
necessary operational expenses as spent locally approved
by the Government. Payment and account will be
opresponden incurred hereunder will be in substantially con-
formance with applicable Government regulations.
The effective date of the amendment should be as of the effective
date of the contract, 19 May 1961.
2. The above request is corrective in nature as it was not
intended to change the travel expense provision which had been in
effect during his previous contract.
H. E. SEOKS
Chief, "H Support
SECRET
201-253203


19 March 1963
Paul O:
Tichborns original contract provided for travel on an actual
expense basis. This was when he was working on a daily or job
rate basis.
This contract was terminated and a new contract was written
in May 1961. He was given as $8,000 per year, and the reimbursement
for operational travel section reads "This may include per diem in
lieu of subsistence-
None of Tichborn's travel claims have been processed since the
new contract has been effective. All travel claims submitted by
him. starting in June 1961 have been submitted on an actual expense
Finance takes the view that the "This may include per diem-
as restricting Tichborn to per diem only plus of course operational
expenses. Processing Tichborns old accounts on this basis would
require him to refund several hundred dollars.
An amendment to the contract would take care of these old
accounts as submitted.
Options:
1. Get refund from Tichborn
2. Amend contract to cover actual expenses to present
date.
3. Amend contract to cover actual expenses past and
future.
What are your wishes?

6 August 1962
The following information was derived from a transcrip-
tion of a tape made during a meeting with Edward TICHBORN
in early June 1962. In Washington, D.C. The purpose of the
meeting was to debrief TICHBORN concerning his opinions and
experiences gained from a recent trip to El Salvador. TICHBORN
spoke from notes for the first part of his report (pp 1-6)
and answered specific questions for the remainder.

hampy to any that the radio schools start. The

I E CIGI
CONTACT REPORT
MEMORANDUM : of Contact and Conversation
Date 5 June 1962
SUBJECT:
Henry Lojos
1. Messors Dick Ouderkirk and Fortor Goss contacted Subject at the
Shorshan Hotel in room 506 N on 5 June to debrief him on his current travel
in 51 Salvador. Subject will be in Washington until Thursday, 7 June. At
de-
the Subject's request a further briefing will take place Wednesday 6 June
at 0930 hours with the benefit of a tape recorder. Subject believed that
there was sufficient material to warrant a detailed question and answer type
discussion and stated that he preferred this form reporting.
2. During the course of luncheon, at which the majority of the meeting
was conducted, the following items of interest were brought out in conversate
Most topics were discussed in generalities in view of the arranged formal
briefing scheduled for the following morning with a recorder.
a) Subject feels that them is a- chanc for real stability in the Rivera
government with the proper support from the US Government.
b) Subject stated that a alight disparity existed in the direction being
taken between the State Dept (Ambeasador) on the one hand and the cos on
the other. Specifically, Subject believed that cos was supporting elements
too far to the right.
o) The military is apparently a tine "third force" and not aligned with
th. 11 families, but broken up into conservative senior officers and an
emerging more liberal junior officer corps. Subject believed that thore may
be a possibility of getting to the campesinos through the liberal element
of the military, but not tog the 11 families.
d) 11 families are becoming isolated and have neither the full support
of the church, the military, or the government. The attitude toward the
minimum wage rate of the Rivora government seems to be "pay one half as many
twice as much. ". The cooperation of the 11 families is needed for the concost
26/253203


development of the country, but as of now they are all the way Right. As for
the minimum wage concept, the canpension apparently do not grasp it a
meaning.
e) The church is not so far Bight that it supports the 11 families and
it is tending more towards the relative left.
f) The Alliance for Progress has been badly handled, as have some of
the activities of the Peace Corps. Subject believes that. too much has been
promised through propaganda already without corresponding results. He bolioves
the danger of the program falling into ridicule is great if the US continues
to promise only, or continue it helply managl publicly asay program.
g) Discussion of the student University papers yielded Subject's opinion
that they are largely inef'ective because they deal in policies rather
than fact and news items, and because because because the ones
with too good format are obviously US pupotes.
h) Less conversation about Fidel Castro is evident in public, although
the Fidel movement is still to be reckoned with. Recently there has been a
standable by Dr. Ruff
recurances of the Martines - dictator of the 1,0's - good old days when
everybody had a job. This statement was also opgined by some expenses.
3. Subject mentioned that he had both high and low level contacts in
El Salvador and had managed to get a reading of public opinion and private
belief. Apparently it is a mistake for Rivera to delay the inauguration
so long after the election; at which time a favorable image of the Col -
was successfully kept before the public, but which is now wearing off.
4. Subject proposed the following courses of action in certain fields
that were discussed in more depth.
c) Fudio is the best means of communication with the campesinos. Subject
was impressed with the results of the operation run by the Catholic priest
in Bolivia 1 using pre-banned radios. He considers that a similar operation


would be extremely valuable if properly handled.
b) Recommends that the Lf facilities be approached on a millionaire to
ademptions that they le
unlitionaire basis in cooperate with R ressonnable reformat movement. especially the

9 February 1962
MEDORANDUN FOR: Chief, WHD
SUBJECT:
Request from Ambassador Williams, El Salvador
1. While visiting with Ambassador Williams and the cos during my
recent trip to San Salvador the Ambassador mentioned the good work done
by Mr. Henry Lopez whom the Agency had sent to El Salvador for TDIY.
2. The Ambassador was so pleased with the accomplishments of
Mr. Lopez that he asked me to convey to you his desire that Mr. Lopes
by sent again on TDIY.
Hawman
PAUL E. ARNEISON
Chief, WE Support
